<div id="review_630793927" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/630793927" />
    <a title="Ari" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3564852-ari"><img alt="Ari" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1451393828p2/3564852.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/630793927?book_show_action=true">Jun 02, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ari" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ari" href="/user/show/3564852-ari">Ari</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=arc-galley-or-author">arc-galley-or-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer630793927" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12994835861029039997">I think I fell in love just a bit ;))<br/><br/><a href='http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/melissa-landers/review-alienated.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380423826i/844608.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>From time to time I fall in love with a cover – hard, instantly – and I never recover from it. You don’t know how much I just love the Alienated cover and how perfect it is for the story!<br/><br/>The Good:<br/><br/>- Imagining aliens looking like us, a better version of us – smarter, better looking, more advanced in all different ways; for some reason I like this concept, I wouldn’t mind it to be true, LOL.<br/>There were many differences between humans and aliens in terms of li</span>
  <span id="freeText12994835861029039997" style="display:none">I think I fell in love just a bit ;))<br><br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/melissa-landers/review-alienated.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380423826i/844608.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>From time to time I fall in love with a cover – hard, instantly – and I never recover from it. You don’t know how much I just love the Alienated cover and how perfect it is for the story!<br><br>The Good:<br><br>- Imagining aliens looking like us, a better version of us – smarter, better looking, more advanced in all different ways; for some reason I like this concept, I wouldn’t mind it to be true, LOL.<br>There were many differences between humans and aliens in terms of living, eating, behaviour, history, genetics and so on, and I loved discovering more things about Aelyx and his kind. Also there were quite a few funny moments involving some of those differences and characters’ curiosity to learn more about the others.<br><br>- The relationship between Cara and Aelyx. They didn’t want to be paired together, one shadowing the other one, and the start of their relationship is quite rocky. But step by step they are learning to trust each other, to be intrigued by the other’s history and customs and through all the messy journey they fall in love (and it’s all so cute and funny, you can’t believe it).<br>There was this teasing and a bit of fighting and trying to see who was the smart ass of the two of them, all in the best funny way of course, and I found myself laughing out-loud so many times. Also the chemistry between them shouldn’t be left out of this review, as it was present at all times.<br><br>- The comparison with what happened not so long again in terms of racism.. and what probably still happens here and there around the world (don’t pretend that’s not true, ’cause closing your eyes won’t change anything). I found all that disturbing in a realistic kind of way. It’s true, in every scenario I could have in my mind there would be people adoringly stalking the poor aliens and people throwing pebbles at them. There would be horrible media manipulation and there would be casualties. Also there would be hidden reasons behind the possible alliance between the 2 species and lots of people being hurt when this would get messy.<br><br>- The supporting family – you don’t see this much in YA books and I really appreciate it. Maybe parents are not always the best (as the difference in age and thinking is not something that one can ignore), but I like to think that someday I will have a kid that won’t think about me what YA characters think about their mother. And this family sounds like a nice one to have (except for the brother that is mostly a clueless lunatic, or so I thought of him).<br><br>This is the beginning of what I hope to be a great series. I like the characters and the settling and I won’t even bother you with my love for the cover (God, I can’t wait to have a copy in my hands!) and I am really eager to find out more about L’eihr (the alien planet) now that Cara is headed there.<br><br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/melissa-landers/review-alienated.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380334106i/693595.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg">

<div id="review_1823186683" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Frankie Lovely" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/61971658-frankie-lovely"><img alt="Frankie Lovely" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1493240668p2/61971658.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1823186683?book_show_action=true">Apr 07, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Frankie Lovely" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Frankie Lovely" href="/user/show/61971658-frankie-lovely">Frankie Lovely</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61971658-frankie-lovely?shelf=rtc-review-to-come">rtc-review-to-come</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1823186683" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer364588698368548259"><b>3.5 stars<br/>Review to come</b><br/><br/>A solid read overall!<br/><br/>I promise to write up a full review of my likes and dislikes of this book in a few ... but Im going to gush about the author of this book for a minute first :P<br/><br/>I recently read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21793182.Starflight__Starflight___1_' title='Starflight (Starflight, #1) by Melissa Landers' rel='nofollow noopener'>Starflight</a> and loved it ... this is another really cute YA fantasy from this great author!<br/><br/>Melissa Landers is quickly becoming one of those "I will pick up anything she writes" sort of authors.   <span id="freeText364588698368548259" style="display:none"><b>3.5 stars<br />Review to come</b><br /><br />A solid read overall!<br /><br />I promise to write up a full review of my likes and dislikes of this book in a few ... but Im going to gush about the author of this book for a minute first :P<br /><br />I recently read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21793182.Starflight__Starflight___1_" title="Starflight (Starflight, #1) by Melissa Landers" rel="nofollow noopener">Starflight</a> and loved it ... this is another really cute YA fantasy from this great author!<br /><br />Melissa Landers is quickly becoming one of those "I will pick up anything she writes" sort of authors. She is the queen of writing characters that feel their age without becoming "what an out of touch adult imagines a teenager sounds like" (you know what I'm talking about). Her writing is quick and lighthearted and witty without sounding cheesy. Her stories are fun and enjoyable.<br /><br />And this book was another strong representation of Landers talent.<br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_622684737" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/622684737" />
    <a title="Faye, la Patata" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7650833-faye-la-patata"><img alt="Faye, la Patata" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557835753p2/7650833.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/622684737?book_show_action=true">May 23, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Faye, la Patata" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Faye, la Patata" href="/user/show/7650833-faye-la-patata">Faye, la Patata</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=2013">2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=subtle-but-giddy-worthy-romance">subtle-but-giddy-worthy-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=no-instalove">no-instalove</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=sexy-leads">sexy-leads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=1st-in-series">1st-in-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=slow-and-steady-romance">slow-and-steady-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=good-hero">good-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer622684737" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17199203241938348347"><a href='http://thesocialpotato.maryfaye.net/2014/01/01/review-alienated-alienated-1-by-melissa-landers/' rel='nofollow noopener'><b>Filipino readers, you can read this book early! Head over to The Social Potato blog and fill up the rafflecopter form to get a chance to win an ARC of this beautiful novel. We're also giving away a Php 300 Fully Booked Giftcard on the blog!<br/><br/>International readers, you can also get a chance to snag a finished copy of this book via The Book Depository! If you win, we will pre-order for you, and you only need to wait until the release date to wait for your book to arrive! Head over to the blog now to</b></a></span>
  <span id="freeText17199203241938348347" style="display:none"><a href="http://thesocialpotato.maryfaye.net/2014/01/01/review-alienated-alienated-1-by-melissa-landers/" rel="nofollow noopener"><b>Filipino readers, you can read this book early! Head over to The Social Potato blog and fill up the rafflecopter form to get a chance to win an ARC of this beautiful novel. We're also giving away a Php 300 Fully Booked Giftcard on the blog!<br /><br />International readers, you can also get a chance to snag a finished copy of this book via The Book Depository! If you win, we will pre-order for you, and you only need to wait until the release date to wait for your book to arrive! Head over to the blog now to get a chance to win!</b><br /><br />Just in: we're giving away THREE finished copies to US/Canada residents! Join now!</a><br /><br /><em></em>To be completely honest, <em>Alienated</em> was a very surprising read. I was expecting hardcore science fiction that was mildly altered to suit young adult tastes with a bit of romance here and there, but it turned out to be the opposite. It's a fluffy read of two students from two different worlds, one from Earth and one from another galaxy hundreds, probably thousands of light years away, as they learn from each other's cultures and endure the widening protest and violence against the two civilization's mingling of each other. So it has a lot of fluff, a lot of politics, and a lot of science fiction. And you know what else? 
  <strong>
    <em>I LOVED IT!</em>
  </strong>
<br /><br />The plot is actually pretty simple. Aelyx (pronounced A-licks) and two of his friends, Syrine and Eron, are to be sent to Earth in a sort of student exchange, a move that hopes to strengthen the relationship of the two planets. However, the trio has other plans, as they don't want their home to be influenced by the violence and discord human societies have showcased in their history, so they plan to sabotage everything.  He later meets Cara, a human with a passionate and gentle heart and a fiery spirit, and she could just be the key to weakening Aelyx's resolve.<br /><br /><strong>It may seem really cliché and worn-out due to the premise being written a hundred times in other novels, but reading this book, you'll find yourself grinning to yourself anyway, because the book's strongest point isn't the plot – it's the development between Cara and Aelyx as they learn more about each other. I swear, I laughed, I cried, and I grinned like a mad lunatic.</strong> It was so funny to read the alien guy being wary of human customs, of their food, of their sexual advances, of his OWN sexual reactions (to which he would try to recite the human periodic table afterwards... haha!!)... it felt like a learning experience for me, too. Aelyx was an adorable character, and even though as a reader you know he has other agendas, you kind of understand the reasons why he was willing to do what he planned (and honestly, if I were an alien from outer space, I wouldn't bother with humans, too. We're complicated beings =P).<br /><br /><strong>As much as it was heartwarming, there were heartrending scenes too, in which I couldn't help but tear up a bit.</strong> There is a political backdrop here as many people are not keen on having aliens in their midst, and it results to a lot of betrayal and violence, and these take a toll on Cara. <strong>My heart swelled and my throat tightened whenever she would put her head up high despite all the bad things happening to her, and even more when Aelyx saw all of these and blamed himself for it. Sigh. If there's anything this book was, it was one hell of a roller coaster ride.</strong> I felt so connected to the characters that I could feel the emotions overflowing from the pages. Such a spectacular novel, this one.<br /><br /><strong>All in all, this was a great read,</strong> and would be an excellent introduction to the science fiction genre to others out there who are hesitant to try it. It's full of heart and emotions, and a lot of scenes that would make you laugh, cry, and sweat (that making out scene was HOT, BABY!). <strong>2014 will be a great year if all books are of this calibre!</strong></span>
  <a data-text-id="17199203241938348347" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_369159127" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/369159127" />
    <a title="Jana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4033116-jana"><img alt="Jana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1590925674p2/4033116.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/369159127?book_show_action=true">Jul 15, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jana" href="/user/show/4033116-jana">Jana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4033116-jana?shelf=blog-reviewed">blog-reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4033116-jana?shelf=2013-reads">2013-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer369159127" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11005698359628314600">As soon as I heard about ALIENATED, I was dying to get my hands on it. Since reading JLA's Lux series, I've been a massive fan of aliens and think there should be more of them in YA. Hurray for Alienated! This hilarious, light-hearted sci-fi story with passionate romance is definitely going on my Favorites list. It's got everything that you'd want in a story and the only thing that's not so great is that the release date won't be until February next year and I already need the sequel really bad.</span>
  <span id="freeText11005698359628314600" style="display:none">As soon as I heard about ALIENATED, I was dying to get my hands on it. Since reading JLA's Lux series, I've been a massive fan of aliens and think there should be more of them in YA. Hurray for Alienated! This hilarious, light-hearted sci-fi story with passionate romance is definitely going on my Favorites list. It's got everything that you'd want in a story and the only thing that's not so great is that the release date won't be until February next year and I already need the sequel really bad. <br /><br />The world building and description of the planet L'eihr was phenomenal. It's beautifully done and with the author's amazing storytelling skills, you can clearly picture the planet in your head even though we're in Earth most of the time. The whole exchange program thing was fun and very clever indeed. But what I really did like about this was how realistic the author portrayed both the humans and the L'eihrs. What do you think would really happen when you create this exhange program? Obviously not everyone will be happy with it. Everyone's reactions was very realistic and you could see where everyone was coming from. There was a few mysteries and suprising twists scattered which was a brilliant touch. <br /><br />Cara and Aelyx are the main characters that you wouldn't just get enough of. We have dual POV (yay!!!) which enables us to be able to learn about them individually. Cara wasn't some annoying, whiny brat - no, she was clever, actually thinks before she acts and just an all round interesting character. Guys, we have a new sexy alien in the house. AELYX. Oh, Aelyx. He's one of my top book boyfriends and when you read Alienated, you'll know why. At first, he's a bit mysterious and bland, but as we and Cara gets to know him throughout the book, oh he's just the swooniest character ever. He's HOTTTTT. The romance between them was kept at a slow pace, making the swoony scenes between them extra special. And oh boy, we don't get that much kissing, but when we do, it makes up for it. It's honestly one of the sexiest kissing scenes I've ever read in YA. <br /><br />If you're like me, and want believable and hot off the charts romance, Alienated is a must-read. (By the way, I love this book title - very clever and bold) Anyway, Alienated will sure be a hit next year when it releases. Be sure to buy it then! :)<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11005698359628314600" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14360470427970017374"><i>Alienated</i> was kind of interesting and surprising for me. I didn't expect to like it but then I ended up liking it. I definitely want to dive into the second book right now. <br/><br/>Cara was easily a likable character. She is one of the few students in the world selected to help one of the alien students around. That said alien would live with her family and attend school with her. Then when his visit is "over" they switch place.. well, she becomes the visitor at his planet. Sounds like an awesome exchan</span>
  <span id="freeText14360470427970017374" style="display:none"><i>Alienated</i> was kind of interesting and surprising for me. I didn't expect to like it but then I ended up liking it. I definitely want to dive into the second book right now. <br /><br />Cara was easily a likable character. She is one of the few students in the world selected to help one of the alien students around. That said alien would live with her family and attend school with her. Then when his visit is "over" they switch place.. well, she becomes the visitor at his planet. Sounds like an awesome exchange student program - right?<br /><br />Well besides Cara, there's Aelys who didn't expect to be apart of this weird ass program. He never wanted to either. Then him and his friends come up with a plan to sabotage the shit out of this program. I guess the one thing he also didn't expect was Cara.<br /><br />These two were so freaking adorable. I loved them so much. I still feel like this was a show.. I just can't remember it. The show only lasted for like a season and trust me it shook me to my core that it ended. So I was really happy to dive into this book because it definitely reminded me of that. <br /><br />Overall, I loved this book. A lot more than I expected too at least. I can't wait to dive into the second book because this was just so entertaining. I need more from these characters.</span>

<div id="review_598138160" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/598138160" />
    <a title="Jodi Meadows" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4011205-jodi-meadows"><img alt="Jodi Meadows" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1484438142p2/4011205.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/598138160?book_show_action=true">Apr 23, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jodi Meadows" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jodi Meadows" href="/user/show/4011205-jodi-meadows">Jodi Meadows</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer15879314082641718184">First of all, let’s have a look at the beautiful cover. I mean seriously, look at the design and models. They’re amazing!<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1396204290i/9101526._SY540_.jpg' width='274' height='415' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Almost seventeen Cara has it all; a boyfriend, a best friend, loving parents (which she complains about), beauty and perfect grades.   <span id="freeText15879314082641718184" style="display:none">First of all, let’s have a look at the beautiful cover. I mean seriously, look at the design and models. They’re amazing!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1396204290i/9101526._SY540_.jpg" width="274" height="415" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Almost seventeen Cara has it all; a boyfriend, a best friend, loving parents (which she complains about), beauty and perfect grades. When she’s assigned to host a L’eihr (Aelyx) for the intergalactic exchange program and has no choice but accepting, she knows a lot would change in her life. Except she never thought she could actually come to like the guy, or shall I say Alien?<br><br><b>This novel contains an alternative POV.</b><br>This was fun and entertaining, exactly the kind of book that you’ll read to relax and have a good time. It unfortunately features many immature characters that you would like to shake or slap or scream at, due to frustrating and impatience which was the boring part of this book. But since Cara and Aelyx aren’t part of them, it made reading <i>Alienated</i> a lot more enjoyable. Aelyx was my favourite character since the very beginning. I liked seeing his developpement because he actually gets nicer and nicer with every chapter. He’s also truly hilarious when he’s talking all formal and statistical about mating. I laughed out loud quite often.<br><br>The writing was simple and included a couple of alien words referring to some objects and words. It was never confusing though since they were well described or at least explained. <u>I would say that this debut author, Melissa Landers, made a good job on creating a futuristic world and an Alien hero that will heartily charm readers and will just make you want to know more and more of him.</u> <br><br>I look forward to reading the sequel!<br></span>

  <span id="freeText13953439061533233044" style="display:none"><b>4.5/5</b><br /><br />This book was very good. I had been wanting to read it for a long time so I was glad that my library got it. Besides that I really liked it. I thought that Cara was a good character because she was very smart and could stand up to each other. Her best friend though I didn't like toward the end of the book. I loved reading about the L’eihrs and I can't wait to learn more in the 1.5 and 2nd book in the series.<br /><br />Overall, I would definitely recommend this book and series to anyone who loves romance (because Melissa Landers is a great writer of romance apparently), action, sci-fi, and fantasy. <div id="review_1886265633" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1886265633" />
    <a title="Veronique" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12371602-veronique"><img alt="Veronique" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1590509341p2/12371602.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1886265633?book_show_action=true">Jun 01, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Veronique" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Veronique" href="/user/show/12371602-veronique">Veronique</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/18973958-alienated">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12371602-veronique?shelf=r2017">r2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12371602-veronique?shelf=stars-4-0">stars-4-0</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1886265633" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11597695280709059197"><i>"How can we understand what we’ve never experienced and adapt without making mistakes"</i><br/><br/>I have been on the fence about this book for quite a while, pondering whether to read it or not. As it happens, a copy found its way to me and I pretty much read it in one day.<br/><br/>Landers creates a very interesting premise, a story of cultural clashing between humans and aliens, who have only recently met. Three L'eihr come to Earth as exchange students, and the narrative follows one of these, the one going to the </span>
  <span id="freeText11597695280709059197" style="display:none"><i>"How can we understand what we’ve never experienced and adapt without making mistakes"</i><br /><br />I have been on the fence about this book for quite a while, pondering whether to read it or not. As it happens, a copy found its way to me and I pretty much read it in one day.<br /><br />Landers creates a very interesting premise, a story of cultural clashing between humans and aliens, who have only recently met. Three L'eihr come to Earth as exchange students, and the narrative follows one of these, the one going to the US. Aelyx has been 'allocated' to Cara, an ambitious and driven valedictorian, to facilitate his experience and live with her family. His arrival however incites the usual prejudice which sadly escalades and turns only too quickly to violence. Seeing all these big themes dealt on a small scale, that of a teenager, her parents, friends and school, illustrate the obtuseness of people on a personal scale. And it isn't just the humans - no, the L'eihr aren't perfect either.<br /><br />The novel focuses of course on Cara and Aelyx, from their initial mistrust to reluctant friendship. Both have their prejudices too but at least are intelligent enough to try to see beyond these. I enjoyed witnessing how their relationship starts and evolves. There are a couple of points I wasn't too sure but in all, it was a really good book. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11597695280709059197" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16457772228141551227">I really enjoyed this book. So much so that I read it in one sitting and up until pass 1 am on a weekday.   <span id="freeText16457772228141551227" style="display:none">I really enjoyed this book. So much so that I read it in one sitting and up until pass 1 am on a weekday. This book involves an exchange student program with aliens and humans (talk about foreign exchange) and involves a slow burn romance between the two mains, Cara and Aelyx, that though predictable because we are told to expect it, it is actually an amusing romance. I did not like Syrine, but will wait to rant about her until I read the next two books this week. I have had this trilogy on my bookshelf for years and cannot believe it took me this long to read them and I am so glad that my reading resolution is to work on reading off my bookshelf to help clear up more book space, because this one was fascinating! <br /><br />My quick and simple overall: fun and quick and wholly entertaining! <br /></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1155907328" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13623860102676577213">3.75/5 or 4/5 I honestly can't decide which fits it more for me.<br/><br/>So many of my friends here on Booktube have recommended this book to me, and I am so glad I finally picked it up, especially after reading a lot of fantasy up until it. It was the fresh breath I needed with reading. <br/><br/>Cara is a bomb character. I really enjoyed the Debate Team aspect of her life, because I could really see that threaded through her character the entire storyline - I'm glad she didn't lose herself.<br/><br/>I liked Aelyx too. I a</span>
  <span id="freeText13623860102676577213" style="display:none">3.75/5 or 4/5 I honestly can't decide which fits it more for me.<br /><br />So many of my friends here on Booktube have recommended this book to me, and I am so glad I finally picked it up, especially after reading a lot of fantasy up until it. It was the fresh breath I needed with reading. <br /><br />Cara is a bomb character. I really enjoyed the Debate Team aspect of her life, because I could really see that threaded through her character the entire storyline - I'm glad she didn't lose herself.<br /><br />I liked Aelyx too. I am especially glad that this book was a dual perspective story, I think it worked better this way.<br /><br />I would have preferred for them to have a little bit more relationship because the events of what happened towards the end.<br /><br />On the world-building scale, I thought Landers wrote it very originally. I loved learning about this alien species, and how aliens were known in our world society. Everything about the science fiction aspect of the book was highly enjoyable. Can't wait for the second one!</span>
  <a data-text-id="13623860102676577213" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer13682306195318771711">Loved this book and the slow, building romance. The characters are awesome and really like learning about the home world. I found myself craving pot roast, but not bland pot roast. If you're a sci-fi fan, pick this one up.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_581643411" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/581643411" />
    <a title="Celeste_pewter" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16386248-celeste-pewter"><img alt="Celeste_pewter" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1482736744p2/16386248.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/581643411?book_show_action=true">Apr 05, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Celeste_pewter" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Celeste_pewter" href="/user/show/16386248-celeste-pewter">Celeste_pewter</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer581643411&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer581643411" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15205417307668075793"><b>Two-second recap:</b> Alienated is a stunner of a debut novel. <br/><br/>With two engaging lead characters, a star-crossed romance (quite literally in this case!), and an unexpected series of twists, this is a book that is sure to capture the heart of readers everywhere. <br/><br/>***<br/><br/><b>
  <u>Full review:</u>
</b><br/><br/>Since the latter half of 2013, it seems like aliens have been the subject du jour in the world of YA fiction. <br/><br/>Books like Demitria Lunetta’s <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12157407.In_the_After__In_the_After__1_' title='In the After (In the After #1) by Demitria Lunetta' rel='nofollow noopener'>In the After</a> (HarperTeen), Margaret Stohl’s <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11861715.Icons__Icons___1_' title='Icons (Icons, #1) by Margaret Stohl' rel='nofollow noopener'>Icons</a> (Little, Brown BFYR) and Rick Yan</span>
  <span id="freeText15205417307668075793" style="display:none"><b>Two-second recap:</b> Alienated is a stunner of a debut novel. <br /><br />With two engaging lead characters, a star-crossed romance (quite literally in this case!), and an unexpected series of twists, this is a book that is sure to capture the heart of readers everywhere. <br /><br />***<br /><br /><b>
  <u>Full review:</u>
</b><br /><br />Since the latter half of 2013, it seems like aliens have been the subject du jour in the world of YA fiction. <br /><br />Books like Demitria Lunetta’s <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12157407.In_the_After__In_the_After__1_" title="In the After (In the After #1) by Demitria Lunetta" rel="nofollow noopener">In the After</a> (HarperTeen), Margaret Stohl’s <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11861715.Icons__Icons___1_" title="Icons (Icons, #1) by Margaret Stohl" rel="nofollow noopener">Icons</a> (Little, Brown BFYR) and Rick Yancey’s <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16101128.The_5th_Wave__The_5th_Wave___1_" title="The 5th Wave (The 5th Wave, #1) by Rick Yancey" rel="nofollow noopener">The 5th Wave</a> (Putnam), have all explored what it’s like to live in a world where aliens are the invading force, pushing humanity to the brink of extension. <br /><br />But what if the aliens weren’t in fact, an invading force? What if they were just as curious about humans, as we would be about them? And just what if we set up…a student exchange program with them? <br /><br />These are the questions that Melissa Landers seeks to answer in her debut novel, Alienated. Rather than portray aliens as faceless, nameless invaders, Landers introduces us to the L’eihr, a peaceful group of aliens with DNA almost identical to humans, but with one very notable difference: they can’t feel emotion. <br /><br />Two years after making contact with Earth, the L’eihr and Earth have arranged to host a student exchange program for their best and brightest. Cara Sweeney is chosen to host Aelyx, a cold but smart young man, who has ulterior motives for joining the exchange program. <br /><br />As both Cara and Aelyx slowly begin to get acquainted, a wave of anti-L’eihr paranoia pushes them far beyond their comfort zones. Though they turn to each other for support, the secret that Aelyx has been hiding may end up forcing Cara to fight for both herself and her planet. <br /><br />***<br /><br /><b>
  <u>Things that worked:</u>
</b><br /><br />As usual, let’s start with the basics: <br /><br /><b>* Writing/World-building/Plotting:</b><br /><br /><b>Writing:</b><br /><br />Landers writes with an effortless confidence, and her words fly off a page in a way that made reading Alienated incredibly enjoyable. <br /><br />I was especially impressed with her ability to alternate between Cara and Aelyx’s voices in each chapter, using third-person limited. Landers adds enough detail and distinction to make the mindset of both characters distinctive, which is not an easy feat when using that particular narration style. <br /><br /><br /><b>World-building:</b><br /><br />The mythology behind the L’eihr is an incredibly detailed one. Without revealing any spoilers, Landers has definitely created an alien origin story that is rich and complex, and I can’t wait for her to further explore the world in following books. <br /><br />At the same time, Landers has also created a post-L’eihr earth that is completely believable and feasible. I can totally see something like HALO forming in the aftermath of contact with the L’eihrs, and I also look forward to seeing how they’re going to react after the events of the first book. <br /><br /><br /><b>Plotting:</b><br /><br />For a book that covers a fairly significant amount of time – about a year in earth time - the book moves at a brisk pace. Landers does a good job of building up the action slowly, until it hits the climax in the latter half of the book.<br /><br />There’s a fine balance between the day-to-day of Cara and Aelyx’s life – including the gradual unfolding of their romance – and the more explosive elements of the book. I think this will definitely heighten the appeal to reads who want both a sci-fi, and elements of a contemporary YA. <br /><br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>* The characterizations.</u>
</b><br /><br />Cara Sweeny had my heart from the very first page of Alienated, where she proudly admits to retaking AP calculus solely for the purpose of boosting her GPA, so she could secure (a.k.a. steal) the position of valedictorian. <br /><br />This is a girl who knows what she wants, and knows what she needs to do to get it. Cara’s clearly driven and clever, but also not in a way that would make her obnoxious or unlikeable. She’s also curious and empathetic about life and the world around her in a way, which I think would make just about anyone want to be her friend. <br /><br />Even as things get tough as the book progresses – including some incredible peer pressure - she never loses sight of who she is, and what she stands for. I strongly applaud Landers for writing a character with qualities that teenage readers can look up to.<br /><br />All of these sentiments apply to Aelyx, as well. Even though he’s technically emotionless, he’s still empathetic, and more importantly, smart enough to admit when he’s wrong. <br /><br />I especially loved Aelyx’s transition from passionately arguing the beliefs that he held before his stay on Earth, to the realization that he was wrong. He’s so smart when coming to the awareness that he’s been wrong this entire time. <br /><br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>* The socio-economic implications.</u>
</b><br /><br />As someone who works in politics, I loved the fact that many of the issues experienced by Cara and Aelyx are extremely relevant to our current political landscape. <br /><br />Readers will recognize many of the issues being faced by the main characters – e.g. immigration (though, slightly more galactic in this case); cultural conflict; religious diversity, etc. – as ones that are faced by our families, friends and leaders today. <br /><br />But what’s notable about Landers’ incorporation of these issues is her skill at showing both sides of the argument. She always makes it clear – whether through conversation or action – that there are two sides to every issue, and it’s important to respect both sides. <br /><br />I think educators and parents can easily use the issues discussed in Alienated as a way of connecting to general real-world issues at large, and to invoke more classroom discussion after that. <br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>* The romance. </u>
</b><br /><br />Cara and Aelyx’s romance is the perfect example of the slow burn. <br /><br />The two of them take the time to get to know each other, slowly and surely. They talk. They learn things about one another. They do small things for one another, to feel more comfortable in each other’s presence. <br /><br />E.g. Cara basically goes into a cooking frenzy, to make sure that Aelyx has food that he’ll eat and enjoy. Alternatively, Aelyx makes a strong effort to be more human through observing the conversations and actions of others, because he knows it’ll make Cara feel better. <br /><br />I loved the fact that their relationship is something that’s slowly built upon time, so we can see why they go from being slightly suspicious of one another, to falling passionately for one another. I absolutely can’t wait to see where Landers is going to take this romance in the rest of the series. <br /><br /><br />***<br /><br /><b>
  <u>Things that didn’t work/Things to consider:</u>
</b><br /><br />Without giving too many spoilers away, I ultimately felt that the ending was a wee bit too rushed. Characters seemed a little too okay with what I thought was a pretty drastic decision for one of the main characters. <br /><br />However, I also do think that the ending does set up the next book in the series beautifully. <br /><br />***<br /><br /><b>
  <u>Final verdict:</u>
</b><br /><br />Alienated is a charming, intelligent addition to both the science-fiction and YA genres. Melissa Landers has written a novel that is charming and funny, and also incredibly smart. <br /><br />I would recommend this book for readers who are fans of both science fiction, and of contemporary YA. I would also recommend this book for fans of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4684322.Marissa_Meyer" title="Marissa Meyer" rel="nofollow noopener">Marissa Meyer</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4018722.Beth_Revis" title="Beth Revis" rel="nofollow noopener">Beth Revis</a>. <br /><br /><br />***<br /><br /><b>
  <u>Disclaimer:</u>
</b><br /><br />I received an ARC of Alienated from Disney-Hyperion in exchange for an honest review. Thank you!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15205417307668075793" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('t3kaZbKsBnUFpS32cAQ3sA9O9yJj1wQTdv8vM5CN4QrAtbx771td/BOmXAOuWoYyKgDGBZAX6ftd3iu3I2asCA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('kqqITtjIl5+pSQCNpi3vTFMo0uiFyVHa9SPdiCXYvKDlZi5QhT/MFr9KcXh4c17Odmbjz3YJvDLeAtkMljPxog==')})
  }

With Aelyx, her L’eihr boyfriend, back on Earth, working to mend the broken alliance between their two planets, Cara is left to fend for herself at a new school, surrounded by hostile alien clones. Even the weird dorm pet hates her.\n\nThings look up when Cara is appointed as human representative to a panel preparing for a human colony on L’eihr. A society melding their two cultures is a place where Cara and Aelyx could one day make a life together. But with L’eihr leaders balking at granting even the most basic freedoms, Cara begins to wonder if she could ever be happy on this planet, even with Aelyx by her side.\n\nMeanwhile, on Earth, Aelyx, finds himself thrown into a full-scale PR campaign to improve human-L’eihr relations. Humans don’t know that their very survival depends on this alliance: only Aelyx’s people have the technology to fix the deadly contamination in the global water supply that human governments are hiding. Yet despite their upper hand, the leaders of his world suddenly seem desperate to get humans on their side, and hardly bat an eye at extremists’ multiple attempts on Aelyx’s life.\n \nThe Way clearly needs humans’ help . . . but with what?     first = d.getElementsByTagName('SCRIPT')[0],
    n = load.length,
    i = 0,
    go = function () {
      for (i = 0; i < n; i += 1) {

        script.src = load[i];
        first.parentNode.insertBefore(script, first);
      }

    w.attachEvent('onload', go);
  } else {
    w.addEventListener('load', go, false);
